In my view, beneath deluded return lie earnest, solitary, frequent, and resting returns—these are what Zhu Xi calls "the multitude’s having return." Though their ranks vary in excellence, none match Yanzi’s learning of foreknowing the subtle. "Conquering the self for a single day, the world turns to benevolence"—the heavens open as if the clouds have dispersed.

The sage teaches by holding up the highest standard; for those of lesser capacity, one may proceed in order. The *Xiang* says: "In seven days, it returns—this is the course of heaven." The explanation of "seven days" has been given above. Master Cheng says: "Heaven’s movement, with its waxing and waning, is the principle of heaven." Master Hengqu says: "Seven days and nights follow one another without interruption."

Moreover, it is said: "When the end comes, there is a beginning—this is the movement of heaven," which never ceases. To rectify it through stillness—what fixed term could there be? This is movement within stillness, movement that knows no exhaustion. What is more, from the inception to the dissolution of a cycle, from the origin of heaven and earth to the present, it has ever been thus. For stillness gives rise to movement, and heaven, without intent or action, governs nothing. Being perpetually so, how could it ever rest? If one contrives or arranges stillness, how could it endure? From this, it departs.

Master Zhu says: "When *Bo* reaches its extreme, it becomes *Kun*. Yang descends and enters *Kun*. When the extreme moves, yang ascends and emerges, traversing the six yin lines. When it reaches the extreme and returns to the beginning, this is the course of the sun, the moon, and the year. The numbers of heaven, earth, and the Five Phases cannot be defied. And again, it is said to be seven days—this clarifies the origin of pitch and calendar. Thus, the sun, moon, and five planets begin in *Qianniu*. Qi begins at midnight, the calendar begins at the winter solstice, and pitch begins with *Huangzhong*. Yang Xiong grasped this and composed eighty-one chapters to exhaust the numbers of one *yuan*, six *jia*, three systems, nine gatherings, and two hundred forty-two sections. Shao Yong grasped it and thereby elucidated the origins, conjunctions, evolutions, and epochs of the sun, moon, stars, and constellations, exhausting the boundless numbers of heaven and earth’s waxing and waning.

In my humble view, Master Cheng’s explanation of the principle of heaven’s waxing and waning is concise and precise. Master Zhang’s account captures the grandeur of the phenomenon, stating that the yang qi circulates even in the depths of winter without ever ceasing—all deduced from the generative principle of *Qian* and *Kun*. As for Hanshang, he elucidates principle solely through numbers, using the seven-day cycle to infer the origins of pitch, calendar, and hexagram qi, as well as the theory of the winter solstice and midnight. He further cites the *Tai Xuan* and *Huangji Jingshi* to expand upon this. Thus, *Fu* not only clarifies principle but also encompasses number.

Master Zhu has said: "Heaven and earth are fundamentally the circulation of a single qi, manifesting as movement and stillness. In terms of the essence of this circulation, it may simply be called *Qian*, which encompasses all. When divided into movement and stillness, it becomes yang odd and yin even. Whether vast as heaven, earth, sun, moon, and stars, or minute as years, months, days, hours, cold, heat, day, and night, all are encompassed." Thus, the coming of yang and the going of yin in *Fu* fully embodies the meaning of heaven’s movement from end to beginning.

The *Appended Judgments* of the *Book of Changes* says: "*Fu* is small yet discernible among things." A single yang sprouts in the Yellow Palace, beneath the host of yin—its beginning is as fine as a thread of silk. Yet amidst the multitude of yin, it does not intermingle, like a speck of white in darkness. The white is discernible, and the mass of black cannot obscure its whiteness. Like the sun not yet risen above the earth, even when hidden within the earth, it cannot be contained. Viewed through human affairs, it is like Yanzi: though deemed foolish, among the three thousand disciples, none failed to call him worthy. Thus, Master Zhu says: "When the good in a person first sprouts, though small, the multitude of evils cannot suppress it."

Master Xu says: "*Fu* is the incipient moment of returning to goodness. One must, at the first stirring of thought, in what others do not know and only the self knows, carefully examine this incipient moment and return to goodness. Acting in accord with principle, one becomes a noble person; violating principle, one becomes petty. If one fails to discern this clearly, then in matters, a hairsbreadth of deviation leads to an error of a thousand miles. How can one not stand in awe?"

Master Cheng says: "Yang has no principle of exhaustion. When it changes above, it is born below. There is no interval where it can be contained—this is its rest." When *Bo* is exhausted, it becomes pure *Kun*. How could there still be yang? If hexagrams are matched to months, this corresponds to the tenth month. In terms of qi’s waxing and waning, yang’s exhaustion forms *Kun*, and yang’s return forms *Fu*—yang is never exhausted. Thus, the tenth month is called the "yang month," lest one doubt the absence of yang.

Master Cheng Bozi said: "The gloss of *xi* as 'birth' refers to one matter: when there is rest, one matter is born, with no interruption in between." Master Zhu further said: "When *Bo* is exhausted and becomes *Kun*, a single yang immediately arises below without any discontinuity. This reveals that heaven and earth have no place of rest. For example, in a month of thirty days, the single yang of *Fu* is divided into thirty parts. It gradually accumulates from these thirty days, one part at a time. From the *Xiaoxue* period after the tenth month, with each central qi, one part of yang is born daily. As one part is extinguished above, one part is born below. In all cases of yin and yang’s generation, one line corresponds to one month. Only after thirty days are fulfilled does that space become complete, forming one line. Now, the *Kun* hexagram is not devoid of yang—its beginning is merely exceedingly subtle. Before that space is filled to form a line, it is not that *Kun* is purely yin without yang. This is not an abstruse matter, yet Yichuan did not explain it clearly to others, compelling them to undertake a great endeavor. Initially, a few words were lacking to convey the gradual waxing and waning, the inseparability of yin and yang."

Master Zhu says: "The single yang of *Fu* does not arise suddenly. Rather, it accumulates from the *Kun* hexagram. It is not that at the midnight of the winter solstice, the yang suddenly arises. Precisely at the midpoint of *zi*, the calculation of that single yang is completed. After the midpoint of *zi*, the second yang begins to arise, gradually forming two yang. After a month, it becomes *Lin*. Master Zhu further said: "From *Guan* to *Bo*, thirty days pass before *Bo* is exhausted. From *Bo* to *Kun*, another thirty days pass before *Kun* is complete. Over thirty days, yang gradually grows, reaching one yang at the winter solstice. The second yang then begins to diminish yin. Each day, one-thirtieth of yin is exhausted, and after a month, it is fully exhausted. As yang grows, each day one-thirtieth of yang is added, and after a month, one yang is fully formed. During the exhaustion, each day of twelve *ke* gradually diminishes in full. One day exhausts one-thirtieth. The gradual growth of yang is likewise—each month’s crescent and full moon reveal how yin and yang thus successively arise."

The yin does not deplete all at once, nor does the yang grow all at once. In the ninth month, yin reaches its extreme, and yang has already begun to arise below, though it has yet to take form. The six yang lines divide into six segments, and each segment further divides into thirty parts. Even the smallest segments must accumulate incrementally, and only at the winter solstice does one yang line fully form. The top line of *Bo*’s *nine at the top* is divided into thirty parts, with one part depleted each day until the end of the ninth month, when it is fully exhausted. The same applies to yin.

This can be understood by observing gestation, though the sages did not speak of it thus. It is further said: Within the space between heaven and earth, qi exists in six layers. This qi ascends and descends, rising and falling. At the winter solstice in the eleventh month, it begins to arise from the lowest layer, ascending all the way to the sixth. By the fourth month, when it reaches the heavens, the yang qi, having just fully formed, begins to dissipate. It is this single qi that rises and falls in endless circulation, moving through the six layers. All arising is but yang qi. When yang grows by one part, it does not borrow from yin; rather, where yang dissipates, yin naturally emerges.

Thus, the arrival of yang is *Fu* (Return), and *Fu* is the original state of things. The arrival of yin is *Gou* (Stain), and *Gou* is but an accidental encounter. It is further said: In the hexagram *Fu*, the single line at the bottom is movement. Master Cheng said: "Since ancient times, Confucians have spoken of stillness as revealing the heart of heaven and earth, but I alone say that movement reveals it." Someone asked: "Is this not seeking stillness within movement?" He replied: "Indeed. Yet it is most difficult to speak of a 'movement' before joy, anger, sorrow, and pleasure have arisen. Stillness may be spoken of, but how can one apply the word 'movement'? Stillness must involve some thing to be called so—this is where the difficulty lies. What is stillness like?" He said: "It cannot be called 'nothing,' yet there is awareness. If there is awareness, then it is movement—how can it be called stillness? One who speaks well of the heart can observe the heart of heaven and earth in this."

I say: Before thoughts arise, it may indeed be called stillness. Master Zhu said: "The movement of heaven flows without a moment’s interruption—how could there be a month without yang? Yet once it reaches fullness, it transforms; once it transforms, it changes. The great cycle spans a year and a month; the small cycle, a day and an hour—all follow this pattern. Like a tree whose leaves yellow and fall, the moment they fall, new buds have already sprouted. Trees that remain green in winter first grow new buds before their old leaves fall. When it comes to transformation, heaven and earth are never without change—not only in a year, but in a month; not only in a month, but in a day; not only in a day, but in an hour. It is only that people do not perceive it."

Someone asked: "Why does the *hard fruit* not fall?" He replied: "Simply by not falling, it contains the principle of life. As Master Yichuan said: 'Yang has no principle of complete exhaustion; when it transforms above, it arises below.' *Nine at the top* of *Bo* is the image of the old yang above, the hard fruit. Earlier scholars spoke of peach pits and apricot kernels: the kernel inside the pit, when planted, sprouts—hence it is called *qi*. The kernel is the heart of heaven and earth in generating things; it is not a dead thing. The *Yi* speaks of *qi* only in the hexagrams *Fu* and *Qian*, revealing the heart of heaven and earth in generating things. From the first yin’s dissipation, *Qian* advances to *six in the fifth*, reaching its extreme. *Qian* represents wood and fruit; the yang essence solidifies above, and the *hard fruit* is the greatest of solid things—it appears when *Bo* reaches its extreme. When it reaches the top, it turns downward, and *Gen* inverted becomes *Fu*. Yang arises within the earth, then grows and becomes *Qian*—this is the image of the *hard fruit* that does not fall."

Master Cheng said: "*Fu* speaks of *qi* days to return—when things reach their extreme, they must reverse. This is the principle: there must be life and death, beginning and end. As it says: 'Bending and stretching, coming and going—it is only principle.' One must not take the qi that has just bent as the qi that is now stretching. It is naturally ceaseless. When things disperse, their qi is exhausted, and they cannot return. This is the principle of the original source. Heaven and earth are like a great furnace, melting and refining everything to exhaustion. How could the qi that has already dispersed return to the workings of creation? It is the life-generating qi that is used, not the already-dispersed qi. It is like the sea tide: when the sun rises, it ebbs; when the moon rises, it flows—not that the already-ebbed water becomes the tide."

Master Zhu said: "*Seven days* is taken only for the meaning of seven; *eight months bring misfortune* takes the meaning of eight, calling it *return*. It is not that the yang of the past is brought back anew to regenerate the old. What has passed is gone; the new naturally arises from it. The great virtue is earnest in transformation, flowing like a river without ceasing—how could it rely on the already-dissipated qi as the resource for what is now arising? It only shows that it perishes there and arises here, thereby revealing the image of its coming and going."

Master Cai said: "Yang’s dissipation begins in the month of *Jianwu* (the fifth month) as *Bo*, and by the month of *Jianzi* (the eleventh month), it becomes *Fu*. The hexagram passes through seven lines, and the months pass through seven months. It does not speak of months but of days, just as in the *Book of Songs*: 'the first day, the second day.' Mr. Guo of Lushan said: '*Qian*’s *initial nine* returns at *jiazi*; the work of the year begins at the midnight of the winter solstice. The movement of the seven celestial bodies returns to the beginning of *Ox* (the lunar lodge), extending to the records of calendrical pitch-pipes. The sequence of the four seasons all reaches this point—thus the Yellow Bell is the root of all things. Therefore, when yang rises by one, all things are born; when yin rises by one, all things die. Their reversal and return complete the six positions, and the seasons are formed."

The *Yi* takes stillness as its root; heaven and earth take non-intention as their heart. Stillness follows *Kun*; movement follows *Zhen*. Thunder within the earth is the end of stillness and the beginning of movement.

*Fu* governs movement, not stillness; *Shun* governs stillness, not movement. Master Li of Shizhai further stated: "A single yin arises at *wu*, and the sun travels the southern celestial path. As soon as it reaches the southernmost point, it returns; upon returning, a single yang arises at *zi*, and the sun travels the northern celestial path—this is the winter solstice. Yet the initial yang is as faint as a thread, insufficient for action. It must pass through seven days to attain the number of *shaoyang* within the single yang, gaining three and a half parts out of fifteen. Only then does yang grow robust enough for action. Thus it is said: 'After seven days, the celestial movement returns.' The *hexagram* *Zhen* arises from the firm below, and life cannot be restrained. Only when plants wither and fruits fall to the earth do buds split their sheaths and the impulse of life return. *Yu*’s compliance in movement follows principle before qi; *Fu*’s movement in compliance follows qi before principle."

Master Liu said: "The celestial movement cycles through twelve stages: yin traverses six, and yang traverses six. When yin reaches six and yang loses its position to seven, yang returns to its proper place. This is the cycle of the twelve celestial stages, revolving endlessly. The same pattern applies to years, months, days, and hours." Hanshang said: "Judging by the waxing and waning of the *Qian* and *Kun* hexagrams, a single day from noon to midnight returns to the *zi* hour; a single year from the fifth month to the eleventh month returns to the *zi* month. In terms of one cycle, from the *wu* year it takes nearly seven years to return to the *zi* year. The movement of the celestial Dao naturally follows this pattern, forming a single cycle. Divided into years, months, days, and hours, it is invariably the same. Thus the sixty hexagrams correspond to 360 days, with each pair of hexagrams separated by seven days. The sages preserved the 'seven days’ return' in the *Fu* hexagram to clarify the *qi* of the hexagrams."

Someone asked the foolish one: "How does Master Shao’s *solstices* relate to exhalation and inhalation?" The reply: "After the winter solstice is exhalation; after the summer solstice is inhalation. Exhalation brings forth all things; inhalation draws them in. One year is one exhalation and inhalation—the great opening and closing of heaven and earth. After midnight is exhalation; before dusk is inhalation. Exhalation and inhalation unite yin and yang, forming a single whole in humans. In one day and night, a person has 13,600 breaths. Daytime exhalation responds to all affairs; nighttime inhalation brings the silence of the myriad sounds. Heaven and earth return to the single body, where exhalation and inhalation depend on speech and silence. *Fu* and *Gou* alternate, yang ascends and yin begins to yield. Thus, in the great process of transformation, one *yuan* of 129,600 years is no more than a single year’s span."

*Tianyuan Fawei*, Scroll Fifteen, concludes.

*Tianyuan Fawei*, Scroll Sixteen, compiled by Bao Yunlong Jingxiang of Luzhai, collated by Fang Hui Wuli of Xugu.

**On the Origins of Numerology**

The study of numerology began with Fuxi, who drew the trigrams based on the *Hetu* (River Chart). Over seven hundred years later, Yu governed the floods and obtained the *Luoshu* (Luo River Writing). Another eleven hundred years passed before Jizi composed the *Hongqian*, clarifying the nine categories of the *Luoshu*. Confucius was born in the twenty-first year of King Ling of Zhou (gengxu), five hundred seventy years after Jizi. At seventy, he appended the *Xici* to the *Book of Changes*, elucidating the numerology of the *Hetu* within the fifty-five. Another fifteen hundred years passed before the *Huangji Jingshi* (Supreme Principles Governing the World) emerged. Its numerology did not devolve into mere elaboration because it was rooted in Fuxi’s pre-cosmic trigrams and their derivations. Those who do not speak of numerology find the pre-cosmic sufficient to encompass it. Thus, the transmission of numerology traces back: Fuxi received it and drew the trigrams; Confucius received it and expounded the *Dayan* (Great Expansion); Shao Yong (Kangjie) received it and composed the *Huangji Jingshi*. Its origins and evolution are ever more evident.

As for Yang Xiong’s *Tai Xuan*, Wei Yuan’s *Yuan Bao*, and Sima Guang’s *Qianxu*, they grasped only one facet of the *Changes* and did not attain its ultimate depth. Yet the numerology of the *Huangji Jingshi* is rarely mastered in the world, for its roots lie in *qi*, and its myriad transformations are difficult to fathom—unlike principles, which, once clarified in the mind, remain constant and easy to uphold. Thus, Confucius taught people only to "exhaust principle and fulfill nature to reach destiny." When principle is clear, numerology is contained within it. Yet if numerology is unclear, principle is not easily refined.

Confucius said: "My Way is threaded by one." This suffices. Master Zhu said: "The Supreme Ultimate is principle; yin and yang are *qi*. Movement and stillness are the mechanisms upon which they ride. *Qi* moves, and principle moves with it." Master Cai said: "*Qi* is numerology. In the obscure and boundless, before the first signs emerge, lies the origin of numerology. The division of the One into Two marks the separation of numbers." I say: Before the Supreme Ultimate moves, *qi* is not yet manifest—how could numerology exist? Yet within the steadfast One, the Three are already latent. At the first stirrings of yang’s movement, a faint and indistinct numerological essence arises within, though it remains unmanifest. Where movement becomes evident, the One becomes distinct. When movement stabilizes and stillness ensues, the Two emerges. When stillness reaches its extreme and movement resumes, the Three is born. When movement reaches its extreme and stillness returns, the Four appears. From One to Three, and Three to Nine, yang numbers flow forth, giving rise to all things. From Two to Four, and Four to Eight, yin numbers congeal and solidify, forming the images of all things.

Those who discern the mechanism see clearly and cultivate at the subtle, continuous point of yang. By steadfastly abiding until yin numbers—seven, eight, nine, and six—are reached, no errors arise, and all becomes auspicious. Yet if one’s heavenly mandate is predetermined, yang *qi* may sink into yin *qi*, giving rise to the nature of *qi*-quality. The noble person seeks to transform this by expanding and nurturing the yang goodness of principle. Thus, sages and worthies do not speak of destiny, focusing instead on principle to uphold the world’s teachings. Yet ultimately, they cannot escape it.

The *Book of Changes* speaks of Four Greatnesses, which, together with the sage, make Five. Nothing surpasses heaven and earth in modeling the law; nothing surpasses the four seasons in facilitating transformation; nothing surpasses the sun and moon in displaying luminous images; and nothing surpasses milfoil and tortoiseshell in bringing about the auspicious and inauspicious in the world. Heaven and earth, the four seasons, the sun and moon, milfoil and tortoiseshell—all are manifestations of numerology. Without sages, how could one know heaven and earth as Three and Two, the four seasons as seven, eight, nine, and six, the days as one month, the *Hetu* as two, the *Luoshu* as ten, the tortoiseshell as nine, or the use of forty-nine out of fifty? This is the preparation of things for use, the creation of implements for the benefit of the world—nothing surpasses the sage, who dwells at the center and presides over all.

Thus, it is said: "The sage emulates, images, and models them." It is also said: "The *Changes* has four images, by which it reveals." Before Fuxi, there were no *Hetu* or *Luoshu*, only the natural *Changes* of heaven and earth. Thus, the *Hetu* is the *Changes* drawn by heaven and earth. The *Changes* is yin and yang, ceaseless transformation and alternation. Principle and numerology are inseparable—all are the natural *Changes*. At the dawn of chaos, when people were simple and most knowledgeable, heaven displayed these numbers through the sun, moon, and stars above, while earth presented them through the *Hetu* and *Luoshu* below. Fuxi, the first to arise, revealed these numbers to humanity. From Yao, Shun, Yu, Tang, Wen, Wu, the Duke of Zhou, and Confucius, they were transmitted in an unbroken line to the present. Branches and leaves are drawn from the root, and within branches and leaves, the root is sought. Though myriad transformations differ, the One remains. Those with insight should devote themselves to this.

I note: The *Records of the Grand Historian* states that Fuxi first drew the eight trigrams, created written characters, and replaced knotted cords. The Yellow Emperor’s teacher, Da Nao, investigated the essence of the Five Phases and first devised the *jiazi* (sexagenary cycle). He commanded Rong Cheng to create the calendar and establish numerology. Bamboo from Xiegu was used to listen to the phoenix’s song: the male’s six cries became the six *lü* (yang pitches), and the female’s six cries became the six *lü* (yin pitches). From the harmonious sounds of *gong* and *shang*, the numerology of *lü* and *lü* arose. Before Wu Huai and Tian Huang, records are distant and obscure. The *Spring and Autumn Annals* states that from the beginning of creation to the capture of the lin, nearly 3,276,000 years passed.

The ten epochs span nearly seventy-six thousand years. Had Fuxi not drawn the trigrams and established numerology, how could generations be recorded? Cai Jitong remarked that Shao Kangjie’s calculations originated with Fuxi—this must be thoroughly understood. Master Zhu said: "He merely perceived a principle and drew a few strokes; how could he have arranged them with such swift ingenuity? Had he arranged them one by one, it would not have been the intent of Heaven." The *Records of the Grand Historian* states: "Fuxi was most pure and sincere; he created the eight trigrams—where would there be such swift and ingenious arrangement?"

It further says: The Five resides at the center, serving as the *qi* of Heaven and Earth in equilibrium. The celestial Five dwells at the pole of the celestial sphere, threading through the four seasons; the terrestrial Five resides at the center of the Yellow and Luo Rivers, governing the four directions. In the diagram, five points represent Earth at the center. The outer four points are: Water in the north, Fire in the south, Wood in the east, and Metal in the west.

Within the *wu-si* pitch, the *Huangzhong* note holds the central position. The notes of the four seasons—*jue* in spring, *zhi* in summer, *shang* in autumn, and *yu* in winter—each differ, except for this central note, *gong*. Jing Fang’s pitch regulator consists of twelve strings, with the central string as *Huangzhong*, remaining unmoved; the twelve strings then resonate in response. The Five resides at the center of the twelve months, and when doubled, the Five never departs from the center.

The numbers of Heaven and Earth total fifty-five. The *Dayan* calculation uses fifty, with the central Five as the *qi* of Heaven and Earth in equilibrium. The void at the center, formless and undifferentiated, is the Supreme Ultimate. When it divides, the first signs of form and transformation emerge—this is the primordial *qi* of Heaven. The initial transformation emerges in the north to generate Water, hence Water’s number is one. This "one" as a number derives from its status as the first transformation.

The second transformation emerges in the south to generate Fire, hence Fire’s number is two. This "two" as a number derives from the second transformation of one. The third transformation emerges in the east to generate Wood, hence Wood’s number is three. This "three" as a number derives from the third transformation of one. The fourth transformation generates Metal in the west, its number four, likewise deriving from the fourth transformation of one. Though two, three, and four all derive their names from one, they are collectively called the "generative numbers." Yet this one, having initially emerged from the Five to generate, ultimately returns to the Five to complete its internal formation. Internal and external, generation and completion, are unified in the Five Phases. Thus it is said: Earth is the *qi* of equilibrium, the essence, the ruler of the Five Phases. The Five generates and completes itself, initially requiring nothing. That which is completed by the Five is also doubled to become ten.

In the *Luo River Writing*, whether vertical, horizontal, or curved, all do not depart from three and five—this is the same principle. This celestial number Five, multiplying without decline and entering without loss, accomplishes transformations and moves spirits.

The *Dayan* number is fifty, of which forty-nine are used. The *ce* of *Qian* number 216, and the *ce* of *Kun* number 144, together total 360, corresponding to the days of a year. The *ce* of the two hexagrams total 11,520, corresponding to the number of all things.

Master Shao said: The *Dayan* number is the origin of calculation methods. Thus, the foundation of calculation arises from nothing more than squares, circles, curves, and straight lines. Yang has no ten; yin has no one. Multiplication is the generative number; division is the dissipative number. Though calculation methods are many, they do not exceed these.

Zhang said: Yin and yang are nothing more than waxing and waning; calculation is nothing more than multiplication and division. Multiplication is the application of two. Squares, circles, curves, and straight lines are the four forms. The *Dayan* employs the Four Images as the origin of calculation. Yin ascends and yang descends within the Four Images, resulting in six.

This fool says: Seeking it in the Primordial Heaven, the circle of Heaven has the number three, and its transformations proceed: three to six, six to seven, seven to nine. The square of Earth has the number four, and its transformations proceed: four to eight, eight to six, six to nine. Heaven becomes Earth, Earth becomes Heaven. The interweaving of curves and straight lines, their numbers interlocking and alternating, yield inexhaustible transformations.

The *Yi* has its methods: *Qian* uses the old yang nine, *Kun* uses the old yin six. The *Dayan* uses four, the number of the Four Images. Four multiplied by nine yields thirty-six, the *ce* number of one line in *Qian*. Six multiplied by thirty-six yields 216, the *ce* number of one hexagram in *Qian*. Alternatively, multiplying thirty-six by six also yields this number. Four multiplied by six yields twenty-four, the *ce* number of one line in *Kun*. Six multiplied by twenty-four yields 144, the *ce* number of one hexagram in *Kun*. Alternatively, multiplying twenty-four by six also yields this number.

Thirty-six multiplied by four also corresponds to the *ce* of the two hexagrams. Thirty-two yang hexagrams have 192 yang lines, each line thirty-six. Thirty-two yin hexagrams have 192 yin lines, each line twenty-four. Multiplying 216 by thirty-two: thirty-two times two hundred yields 6,400; thirty-two times ten yields 320; thirty-two times six yields 192. Combined, they total 6,912—the number obtained by multiplying 216 by thirty-two.

Multiplying 144 by thirty-two: thirty-two times one hundred yields 3,200; thirty-two times forty yields 1,280; thirty-two times four yields 128. Combined, they total 4,608—the number obtained by multiplying 144 by thirty-two. This explanation is indeed detailed and clear.

Moreover, each yang hexagram contains 216, and multiplying this by the thirty-two yang hexagrams likewise yields 6,912. Each yin hexagram contains 144, and multiplying this by the thirty-two yin hexagrams likewise yields 4,608. Combined, they total 11,520—is this not simpler and easier?

The *Yijing* employs the old to enact change, hence the counting rods of *Qian* and *Kun* are used. Yet if one combines the counting rods of the two lesser hexagrams from the two Wings, the result is the same. This pertains to a fundamental principle in the study of the *Yijing*, which scholars must not overlook.

Confucius appended this method to the *Yijing*, yet later Confucians failed to explain it with clarity and concision. Shao Kangjie once received this transmission from Chen Tuan, but over time forgot it. One night, he was instructed in a dream and regained it—yet even this was difficult, let alone for later students. Now I am old, and after delving into these calculations, I have recorded them in detail here. If students of the *Yijing* grasp this, then the numbers may be effortlessly unraveled.

The numbers beneath the earth cannot be reckoned. Yet the old and young of yin and yang, of heaven and earth and humanity, and the sixteen images of four-by-four can all be deduced by analogy. Only the numbers beneath the earth remain hidden and difficult to infer. Thus it is said: the subtle images in the world, the forms upon the earth, and the spirits dwelling in the unseen—none are not bound to number; it is merely that people do not perceive them.

The correct tones and numbers operate upon the earth and no further, for on the summer solstice, the sun rises in *yin* and sets in *xu*. Thus the three hours of *hai*, *zi*, and *chou* descend beneath the earth, and their numbers are unseen.

Master Cheng said: Kangjie once exhaustively explored flavors numbering 21,600—something no human could blend. Colors number 28,800—something no human could dye. These are all natural, singular numerical patterns, yet only half are obtained. For yang tones arise only when the sun emerges above the earth, and their numbers are reckoned only until the sun sets beneath it. This is all reasonable.

Where there is speech, there is form; where there is form, there is shadow concealed. How enduring is shadow? The *Guabian* states: one, two, three, four—these numbers lie beneath the earth. At five, they emerge above it. Only then do the beginnings of human life appear, with signs visible to the eye. By six, seven, eight, and nine, they become manifest.

The sages relied on the numbers of heaven and earth to uphold yang and suppress yin. The heavenly number is twenty-five, the earthly number thirty—these are the fundamental numbers of heaven and earth. Earth exceeds by five, hence the *Dayan* number of fifty is employed. Heaven exceeds by ten—why? It is the sages’ way of upholding yang and suppressing yin.

Two and eight, four and six—these are the numbers of earth, yielding only two. One and nine, three and seven, five and five—these are the numbers of heaven, yielding three. Thus the heavenly number is thirty, exceeding earth. Moreover, the yang number three advances to employ the greater number of thirty, while the yin numbers four and six retreat to employ the lesser number of twelve.

From this, we deduce: heaven three and earth two make five; heaven six and earth four make ten; *Qian* nine and *Kun* six make fifteen. *Qian* yields thirty-six, *Kun* yields twenty-four. *Qian* obtains six times seven, totaling 252—the time of generating life. *Kun* obtains only three times six, totaling 108—merely to restrain life.

The sages established these numbers by relying on the flowing transformations of creation—how profound and subtle! Zhen Xishan recorded the words of Cai Yinjun, saying: "The *Yijing*’s images embody the workings of heaven and earth. The *Fan*’s numbers record them. Numbers begin with the odd one; images are completed by the even two. The odd is how numbers operate; the even is how images stand. Thus two by four makes eight—the images of the eight trigrams. Three by three makes nine—the numbers of the nine categories.

Eight by eight, multiplied again by eight, yields 4,096, and the images are complete. Nine by nine, multiplied again by nine, yields 6,561, and the numbers are exhaustive. The *Yijing*’s images were revealed through four sages, while the *Fan*’s numbers were bestowed upon Yu the Great by the gods, yet they were not transmitted. Later scholars, ignorant of the origins of images and numbers, either derived numbers from images or contrived images from numbers, forcing interpretations and obscuring the natural numerical patterns.

The *Yijing*’s eight trigrams, when expanded, form 4,096 images—Jing Fang exhaustively detailed them. Cai Zhongmo said: "My late father said that the *Luoshu* is the origin of numbers. Without understanding numbers, one cannot discuss images. Without understanding images, one cannot discuss numbers. The two cannot exist without each other. Images are employed through the even, and when there is resonance, it is auspicious. Numbers are employed through the odd, and when there is opposition, it is inauspicious.

The even represents the mutual opposition of yin and yang as images. The odd represents the alternating operation of yin and yang as numbers. One is the ancestor of nine; nine is the ancestor of eighty-one. One and nine form a beginning and end as one—just as the year begins and ends at the winter solstice. The nine numbers divide into nine circles; when rotated and counted, the eight solar terms are complete.

Two by two marks *Lichun*; three by three, *Chunfen*; four by four, *Lixia*; five by five, *Xiazhi*; six by six, *Liqiu*; seven by seven, *Qiufen*; eight by eight, *Lidong*; nine by nine, *Dongzhi*. When the nine numbers conclude, one is reborn—generation upon generation without end. Yin ends and yang begins; day ends and night begins; the year ends and spring begins. The end of the former heaven and earth is the beginning of the latter—all without departing from the numbers of the *Hetu* and *Luoshu*.

One by nine makes nine; nine by nine makes eighty-one; eighty-one by nine makes 729; 729 by nine makes 6,561—and the numbers are complete."

The movement of odd numbers establishes the foundation for the forms of even numbers. Thus it is said: the eight trigrams and nine palaces serve as each other’s exterior and interior.

Someone asked about the primordial numbers. Master Zhu replied: *The Great Commentary* has already explained this in detail. The *Kun* hexagram of Earth is the ancestor of the sixty-four hexagrams. The *Hetu* and *Luoshu* are the origin of numbers, the source from which the sages drew the trigrams.

One view holds: The Supreme Ultimate is the origin of principle, while the *Hetu* and *Luoshu* are the ancestors of numbers. From Heaven One to Earth Ten, Fuxi used the numbers of the *Hetu* to draw the trigrams. The fifty-five are the numbers through which Confucius elucidated the numbers of heaven and earth. The fifty of the *Dayan* are the numbers of the milfoil stalks. The 360 of *Qian* and *Kun* are the numbers of the annual cycle. The 11,520 are the numbers of the myriad things—all are primordial numbers. The numbers of the *Hetu* and *Luoshu* encompass all without exception.

King Wen ordered the *Yijing*, placing *Qian* and *Kun* at the beginning. The alternation of yang’s odd and yin’s even lines begins with the division of the *Qian* and *Kun* hexagrams. Thus, when Fuxi drew the primordial trigrams, he began with *Qian* and ended with *Kun*, enclosing the sixty-two hexagrams within them. This is because the numbers of all things under heaven are encompassed within *Qian* and *Kun*.

*Qian* is Heaven, and its number begins with one. One contains three, and three times three makes nine. All the odd numbers of the world—one, three, five, seven, nine—are derived from this. Thus, the Dao of *Qian* completes the male, giving rise to the *Zhen*, *Kan*, and *Gen* trigrams, which disperse through the four seasons. Whether human or thing, all receive the qi of *Qian*.

*Kun* is Earth, and its number begins with two. Three times two makes six, containing twelve lines in its midst. All the even numbers of the world—two, four, six, eight, ten—are derived from this. Thus, the Dao of *Kun* completes the female, giving rise to the *Xun*, *Li*, and *Dui* trigrams, which disperse through the four seasons. Whether human or thing, all receive the qi of *Kun*.

One odd and one even, forming yin and yang, the male and female interlock—all through the numbers of four nines, four sixes, four sevens, and four eights. Generation and transformation flow abundantly within, circulating without cease. Counting forward or backward, all movements converge with these numbers.

The Dao of Heaven moves left in sequence, which is why the five phases generate one another. The Dao of Heaven moves right in reverse, which is why the five phases overcome one another. Overcoming is the means by which they complete one another. Thus it is said: The numbers of the *Yijing* are completed through reversal. *The Commentary on the Trigrams* states: The *Yijing* counts in reverse. It also says: Counting what has passed is sequence; knowing what is to come is reversal. This is what it means.

Master Shao said: Before thoughts arise, even spirits and gods do not know. If not from me, then from whom? Master Yi said: Only with Kangjie did numerology fully attain principle. Master Liu Yunzhuang said: The lines of the *Yijing* arise from the Supreme Ultimate, and thus its principles are the most refined under heaven. The *Yijing* originates from the *Hetu* and *Luoshu*, and thus its numbers are the most mutable under heaven. Principle is established only when it has something to rely upon; though it does not depend solely on the numbers of the *Hetu* and *Luoshu*, it also does not depart from them.

He also said: Ten is two fives, or three threes with one added. Subtract three from ten and you get seven; subtract two and you get eight; subtract one and you get nine; subtract four and you get six. Six is then increased by four, nine by one, and seven by three. Advancing and retreating, expanding and contracting—all movements converge with these numbers. The four images do not depart from ten.

In terms of division: one divides into two, two into four, four into sixteen, sixteen into thirty-two, and thirty-two into sixty-four. Thus it is said: Dividing yin and dividing yang, alternating the yielding and the firm. Ten divides into a hundred, a hundred into a thousand, a thousand into ten thousand, and so on—ten ten-thousands into a hundred thousand, ten hundred-thousands into a million, ten millions into ten million, ten ten-millions into a hundred million, and below a hundred million: *shu*, *rang*, *gou*, *jian*, *zheng*, *zai*, and *ji*. Fifteen names in all, yet none depart from ten.

Roots have trunks, trunks have branches, branches have leaves. The larger they grow, the finer they become; the finer they become, the more numerous they grow. Yang, beginning with *Zhen*, grows until *Qian* and then divides; yin, beginning with *Xun*, arises until *Kun* and then contracts. Growth, division, decline, and contraction—this is simply the movement of the ten numbers.

Thus, Master Cheng said: Two and five combine to accomplish the work of yin and yang. Master Shao said: *Qian*, *Kun*, *Kan*, and *Li* are the ancestors of the thirty-six hexagrams. *Xun*, *Dui*, *Gen*, and *Zhen* are the ancestors of the twenty-eight hexagrams. *Qian*, *Kun*, *Kan*, and *Li*, along with the doubled hexagrams *Zhongfu*, *Yi*, *Xiaoguo*, and *Daguo*—eight hexagrams in all that do not change—are the ancestors of the thirty-six hexagrams. The thirty-six hexagrams are the two sets of eighteen hexagrams in the upper and lower canons.

The *Dui*, *Xun*, *Zhen*, and *Gen* trigrams are transformations of the two original hexagrams, and thus are the ancestors of the twenty-eight changing hexagrams. Twenty-eight: among the thirty-six hexagrams, eight do not change, while twenty-eight do. Observing them in reverse yields fifty-six hexagrams. Why then speak of thirty-six hexagrams?

*Qian* is one and *Kun* is eight. Among a hundred numbers, sixty-four hexagrams are taken as the body, and thirty-six as the function. One to ten is complete, and ten to a hundred is complete. *Kun*’s position above yields thirty-six for function, and below yields sixty-four for body. The inner yin lines complete the body’s numbers, totaling a hundred. Ten recedes by eight, and eight eights make sixty-four. Eight recedes by two, and six sixes make thirty-six.

Some hexagrams contain seven within nine: four nines (thirty-six) contain four sevens (twenty-eight). Some hexagrams contain eight within seven: four sevens (twenty-eight) contain seven eights (fifty-six).

Some hexagrams contain sixty-four within eight: this refers to the eight lower hexagrams remaining unchanged while being doubled to form sixty-four—condensing the expansive. There are those where the Dipper contains three within: when the sixty-four hexagrams are observed in reverse, only thirty-six remain—expanding the condensed. Some conceal nine within eight, yielding one eight, two sevens, three sixes, four fives. This is also called the intersecting numbers of four nines, where all nine bodies are concealed within eight. Thus their forms are inexhaustible. Some conceal nine within ten: the Nine Categories contain the numbers of five nines, with nine matters in substance. The Six Adversities attach to the Five Fortunes, so ten is unseen and concealed within nine. When function conceals form, its use is unceasing.

It is also said: *Qian* employs thirty-six hexagrams, so each line also contains thirty-six numbers. *Kun* employs twenty-four hexagrams, so each line also contains twenty-four numbers. The sixty-four hexagrams correspond to a year’s three hundred sixty days. *Qian*’s one hexagram has six lines, each line thirty-six numbers, six lines totaling two hundred sixteen—this is the line count of the thirty-six hexagrams. *Kun* is allotted twenty-four hexagrams, complementing *Qian* to complete the sixty-four. Each line has twenty-four, six lines totaling one hundred forty-four—this is the line count of *Kun*’s twenty-four hexagrams. Together, *Kun* and *Qian* complete three hundred sixty.

Heaven’s numbers employ seven. Of heaven’s ten numbers, seven is for use, three for intersection. Earth’s numbers employ twelve, eight for use, four for intersection. *Qian*’s original single line, multiplied by thirty-six, yields two hundred sixteen. Now adding six to its numbers. *Kun*’s original single line, multiplied by twenty-four, yields one hundred forty-four. Taking one portion to offer *Qian*, it uses only three sixes—one hundred eight—corresponding to the three hours of *hai*, *zi*, and *chou*. One day, one month, one year—all these numbers move beneath the earth and are not employed by humans.

At times, seven of ten parts are used, following heaven’s use, referring to the Ten Celestial Stems. At times, seven, eight, or nine of twelve parts are used, following earth’s use, referring to the Twelve Earthly Branches. Using seven, two hundred ten are for use, one hundred fifty for intersection. Using eight, two hundred forty are for use, one hundred twenty for intersection. Using nine, two hundred seventy are for use, ninety for intersection. Thus it is said: the numbers of days follow heaven, the numbers of hours follow earth. Numbers have excess and deficiency, arising between the two solstices.

From the hours’ two thousand one hundred comes the yang extreme, the surplus of qi. Yang gains six days—these are the mid-month qi of each month. Six becomes twelve, and yang advances twelve days to make one hundred twenty. From the hours’ two thousand one hundred sixty comes the yin extreme, the new moon’s deficiency. Yin contracts six days—these are the new moon’s deficiencies of each month. Six becomes twelve, and yin retreats twelve days to make one hundred twenty, totaling two hundred forty. Paired with twelve to make twenty-four, the great cycle’s standard number is sixty days per division, while the intercalary number is six days per division. These are distributed among the twenty-four qi, with twelve mid-month excesses and twelve new moon deficiencies, totaling twenty-four—dividing the cycle into four. Day and night divide their use, thus employing two hundred fifty-two.

It is also said: numbers have form and function. Form numbers generate beings and belong to earth; function numbers govern movement and belong to heaven. The form number is three hundred eighty-four, comprising sixty hexagrams. The line count is three hundred eighty-four, with four as form, so three hundred sixty lines are for function. Adding the sixty-four hexagrams, preserving *Qian*, *Kun*, *Kan*, and *Li*’s four hexagrams—twenty-four lines—governing the twenty-four qi, then three hundred sixty lines serve as a year’s function. Preserving ninety lines as form, fifteen hexagrams’ two hundred seventy lines are the numbers of heaven and earth’s function—these are the numbers of *yin* opening and *xu* closing. Preserving one hundred lines as form, eighteen hexagrams’ two hundred fifty-two lines are the numbers of earth’s surface function—these are the months from *yin* to *you*, including intercalary months. Excluding the hexagrams of the three palaces *hai*, *zi*, and *chou*, one hundred eight days—form contains function, function contains form.

Preserving the Supreme Ultimate’s form, the remainder is heaven’s function. Preserving heaven’s form, the remainder is earth’s function. Preserving earth’s form, the remainder is humanity’s function. The actual functional number is two hundred sixty-four—this is the number of pitch pipes, humanity, and beings. Two hundred fifty-six is the number of *Kan* and *Li* generating beings, adding four to earth’s form number two hundred fifty-two to make six, so two hundred fifty-six days have three thousand seventy-two hours—all times for generating beings. Beings are born of yang, so only yang strategies are employed. *Qian*’s yang is thirty-six, *Dui*, *Li*, and *Xun* together total eighty-four. *Kun* is twelve, *Zhen*, *Kan*, and *Gen* together total sixty. Altogether, the eight positions’ yang lines total one hundred ninety-two, plus the original generating four numbers of sixty-four, making two hundred fifty-six.

It is also said: of the sixty-four hexagrams, excluding the initial and top lines and using only the four middle lines, two hundred fifty-six are also obtained. Using four positions refers to the four earthly forms. *Kan* has four yin lines, *Li* has four yang lines—thus generation of beings necessarily employs four. *Qian* and *Kun* establish positions above and below, while *Kan* and *Li* mate within them, serving as the masters of generating beings, gestating their essence and spirit. Excluding the initial and top lines and using only the middle lines is because heaven and earth do not generate beings at dawn and dusk but do at midday, and earth’s north and south do not generate beings but do at midday. If *Li* were not preserved, the four yang lines would have no way to receive *Kun*’s yin. If *Kan* were not preserved, the four yin lines would have no way to accept *Qian*’s yang. Thus each excludes four to establish form. Excluding four means they are constantly preserved yet unused, while two hundred fifty-six are employed.

The initial line is the qi of earth, the root of life. In the *Precelestial Chart*, the thirty-two yang and thirty-two yin lines that remain unchanged are the initial lines left unused. The top line is the spirit of heaven, the origin of nature. Thus, the eight pure hexagrams evolve through five generations to become the "wandering soul" of heaven, and the top line of the *Yijing* does not move.

Master Shao said: The *Yijing* possesses variable numbers, and hexagrams possess variable images. Heaven’s number contains three; doubling three makes six, and tripling three makes nine. Nine times nine is eighty-one, the extreme of yang numbers. At its extreme, yang transforms into yin. Earth’s two doubled makes four, and four times four is sixty-four, the extreme of yin numbers. At its extreme, yin transforms into yang.

There are hexagram transformations: one change yields three—*Qian* transforms into *Zhen*, *Kan*, and *Gen*; *Kun* transforms into *Xun*, *Li*, and *Dui*. One change yields eight—*Qian* shifts from *Gou* to *Tai*, and *Kun* shifts from *Bo* to *Pi*. Among the hexagrams of the three outer sons and three outer daughters, one shares the same variable hexagrams, as observed through the casting of yarrow stalks. Obtaining the two elders’ nine-six changes results in *Qian* and *Kun*. Obtaining the two youths’ seven-eight unchanged lines results in *Zhen*, *Kan*, *Gen*, *Xun*, *Li*, and *Dui*.

There are line transformations: for example, *Kun* changes one line to become *Fu*, and when all six lines change, it becomes *Qian*. Another method involves the mutual ascent of one yang line as a transformation, yielding *Fu*, *Shi*, *Jian*, *Yu*, *Bi*, and *Bo*. There are also transformations of two yang lines, comprising fifteen hexagrams, all derived from *Lin*. Transformations of three yang lines comprise ten hexagrams, all derived from *Tai*.

*Qian* changes one line to become *Gou*, and when all six lines change, it becomes *Kun*. Another method involves the mutual transformation of one yin line, generating *Gou*, *Fu*, *Lü*, *Xiaoxu*, and *Dayou*. There are also transformations of two yin lines, comprising fifteen hexagrams, all derived from *Dun*. Transformations of three yin lines comprise ten hexagrams, all derived from *Pi*. These describe transformations of lines and hexagrams.

The eight trigrams’ transformations, eight times eight, culminate in sixty-four. The sixty-four hexagrams’ transformations, sixty-four times sixty-four, culminate in four thousand ninety-six hexagrams. By extrapolating hexagram lines, these are twelve-line hexagrams. Extending to twenty-four lines yields seventeen million seven hundred seventy-seven thousand two hundred sixteen hexagrams.

Furthermore, in the *Precelestial Chart*, one change yields two hexagrams, two changes yield four, three changes yield eight, four changes yield sixteen, five changes yield thirty-two, and six changes complete the sixty-four hexagrams. The square and circular *Precelestial Charts* correspond precisely. Thus, Master Shao states below: "Changes within correspond to responses without; changes without correspond to responses within. Changes below correspond to responses above; changes above correspond to responses below."

*Xun*, *Li*, and *Dui* with twenty-eight yang lines correspond to *Kan*, *Gen*, and *Zhen*’s twenty-eight yin lines. *Kan*, *Gen*, and *Zhen*’s twenty yang lines correspond to *Xun*, *Li*, and *Dui*’s twenty yin lines. *Qian*, *Dui*, *Xun*, and *Kan* occupy the upper position, while *Li*, *Zhen*, *Gen*, and *Kun* occupy the lower. *Qian*, *Dui*, *Li*, and *Zhen* are internal, while *Xun*, *Kan*, *Gen*, and *Kun* are external. As yang wanes and yin waxes, each hexagram mirrors the other, and there is no change without correspondence.

Change follows heaven. Heaven moves leftward, and the sun shifts one degree; the response follows the sun’s daily rightward movement, with heaven responding one degree. All correspond left and right. The sun’s path is marked by stars—*Qian* and *Li*; the moon meets the celestial stems—*Dui* and *Zhen*; fire arises from earth—*Kun* and *Kan*; fire lies hidden in stone—*Gen* and *Xun*. All correspond above and below.

Flying creatures perch on trees—*Li* and *Gen*; walking creatures rely on grass—*Zhen* and *Kun*; heart and lungs connect—*Qian* and *Xun*; liver and gallbladder adjoin—*Dui* and *Kan*. All correspond internally and externally. Thus, in the *Yijing*’s six lines, the first and fourth correspond, the second and fifth correspond, and the third and sixth correspond, always in opposition.

Heaven and earth envelop each other; the female and male summon one another. Heaven is yang, earth is yin; heaven’s pitch corresponds to earth’s tone. Heaven’s voice initiates, and earth responds. *Qian*, *Dui*, *Li*, and *Zhen* reside in the northwest, initiating earth’s sixteen hexagrams—five, six, seven, eight—in the southeast. They further intersect with the sixteen hexagrams of the southwest—*Pi*, *Dun*, *Song*, and *Shi*—constituting the transformations of heat and cold, day and night, the natures and forms of walking, flying, and plant life. The sixteen hexagrams of movement combine to form two hundred fifty-six hexagrams, their positions aligning with thirty-four changes. All successes and failures, virtues and flaws of animals arise from this.

Earth’s tone harmonizes with heaven. *Kun*, *Gen*, *Kan*, and *Xun* reside in the southeast, harmonizing with heaven’s sixteen hexagrams—one, two, three, four—in the northwest. They further intersect with the sixteen hexagrams of the northeast—*Tai*, *Lin*, *Yi*, *Fu*—constituting the transformations of rain, wind, dew, and thunder, the natures and forms of walking, flying, and plant life. The sixteen hexagrams of vegetation combine to form two hundred fifty-six hexagrams, their positions aligning with thirty-one changes. All flourishing and withering, blossoming and fruiting of plants arise from this.

The hexagrams of the southwest, observed from left to right, pertain to animals. Animals’ lives reside in the head, attached to heaven, with yang arising below. Among the thirty-two hexagrams below, all lines face upward—life resides above. Thus, humans’ heads are above, while birds and beasts are born horizontally. The hexagrams of the northeast, observed from top to bottom, pertain to plants. Plants’ lives reside in the roots, attached to earth, with yin arising above. Among the thirty-two hexagrams above, all lines face downward—life resides below. Thus, humans’ kidneys are below, while grasses and trees grow inverted.

Then, pairing them with the hexagrams of sound: the voices of the sun, moon, and stars belong to heaven’s one hundred twelve hexagrams. The tones of water, fire, earth, and stone belong to earth’s one hundred fifty-two hexagrams.

It is also said: Heaven and earth undergo sixteen changes, totaling six hundred seventy-two divisions of waxing and waning. Heaven’s eight leftward changes, from *Zi* to *Si*, constitute daytime, with three hundred thirty-six as the number of growth.

Earth’s eight rightward changes, from *Wu* to *Hai*, constitute night, with three hundred thirty-six as the number of waning. Together, the two eights make sixteen changes. Heaven governs the body, its eight changes culminating in sixteen. With *Qian* as the master, proceeding from *Yang* onward, two hexagrams correspond to one change, *Tongren* to eight changes, and *Shen* to sixteen changes.

Heaven and earth each divide into eight changes, each yielding the number three hundred thirty-six—the total line count of fifty-six hexagrams. Of the sixty-four hexagrams, excluding *Qian*, *Kun*, *Kan*, *Li*, *Daguo*, *Xiaoguo*, *Zhongfu*, and *Yi*, twenty-four lines remain. Dividing twenty-four by two yields twelve, which is the surplus of six days in the yang count. For the six yin months, totaling one hundred eighty days, excluding the twenty-four lines of *Kun*, *Kan*, *Daguo*, and *Xiaoguo*, twenty-four lines remain. Dividing twenty-four by two yields twelve, which is the deficit of six days in the yin count. Together, the twenty-four lines excluded account for the three hundred thirty-six, combining into six hundred seventy-two divisions of waxing and waning. This also corresponds to the changes of seven, six, five, and four.

The generative numbers of the eight trigrams: *Qian* as one, *Dui* as two, *Li* as three, *Zhen* as four, *Xun* as five, *Kan* as six, *Gen* as seven, *Kun* as eight.

Master Cai states: Yang generates yin, two multiplied by six becomes twelve. Yin generates yang, three multiplied by ten becomes thirty. Thus, *Qian* begins with one, and *Dui* becomes twelve; *Li* becomes twelve and thirty, totaling three hundred sixty; *Zhen* becomes twelve and four thousand three hundred twenty. From *Xun* to *Kun*, all are the generative numbers of odd and even. Applying these to the twenty-four hexagrams and multiplying their generative numbers reveals the total sum. From *Dui* to *Zhen*, the number reaches one hundred fifty-five thousand five hundred twenty. I have calculated this before.

Yang, as one, is odd; yin, as two, is even. Thus, the number of one *yuan* begins with *Qian*, the origin of all counts, just as one year encompasses years, months, days, and hours. After *Qian* comes *Dui*. *Dui* represents the moon, its number two. Expanded, it becomes twelve—one year has twelve months. After *Dui* comes *Li*. *Li* represents the sun, its number three. Expanded, it becomes three hundred sixty—one year has three hundred sixty days. After *Li* comes *Zhen*. *Zhen* represents the hours, its number four. Expanded, it becomes four thousand three hundred twenty—one year has four thousand three hundred twenty hours. These one, two, three, and four are the primordial numbers of heaven and earth’s creation, where yang precedes yin by one.

After *Zhen* four comes *Xun* five. Nothing precedes this as the primordial qi of yin. This is the year count of *Xun Yuan*, expanded to one hundred twenty-nine thousand six hundred, the origin of all counts. *Kan* six follows, representing the month count of *Xun Yuan*, expanded to one million five hundred fifty-five thousand two hundred months. *Gen* seven follows, representing the day count of *Xun Yuan*, expanded to forty-six million six hundred fifty-six thousand days. As for the hour count of *Xun*, it resides in *Kun* eight, further expanded to fifty-five million nine hundred eighty-seven thousand two hundred hours. These five, six, seven, and eight are the concluding numbers of heaven and earth’s completion, where yin follows yang.

Thus, layering and expanding these to eight: *Qian*’s world count is four thousand three hundred twenty, expanded to fifty-five million nine hundred eighty-seven thousand two hundred. *Dui*’s world count is fifty-one thousand eight hundred forty, expanded to six hundred seventy-one million eight hundred forty-six thousand four hundred. Proceeding in order, all can be clearly discerned. Generally, the numbers of *Qian*, *Dui*, *Li*, and *Zhen* encompass those of *Xun*, *Kan*, *Gen*, and *Kun*. From *Zi* to *Si*, the six upper branches belong to *Qian*, called *xiantian* (Prior Heaven). From *Wu* to *Hai*, the six lower branches belong to *Kun*, called *houtian* (Posterior Heaven). Posterior Heaven emulates Prior Heaven. Thus it is said: "Forming the image is called *Qian*; emulating the model is called *Kun*." One may infer the rest from this.

Twelve and thirty are used interchangeably. The twelve months of a year arise from one year multiplied by twelve. The three hundred sixty days of a year arise from twelve multiplied by thirty. The four thousand three hundred twenty hours of a year arise from three hundred sixty multiplied by twelve. The thirty *shi* of a world arise from one *shi* multiplied by thirty. The three hundred sixty months of a world arise from the world count multiplied by thirty. The ten thousand eighty days of a world arise from the world’s days multiplied by thirty. The one hundred twenty-nine thousand six hundred hours of a world arise from the world’s days multiplied by twelve.

The twelve branches and twelve stations correspond to the numbers three, four, two, and six. Doubling twelve yields three, eight, four, and six. The yin number two expands to twelve: twelve branches, twelve hours, twelve months, twelve worlds, twelve hexagrams. *Kun* has twelve lines; humans have twelve components—thus earth’s numbers begin with twelve. The twelve branches are the branch numbers and month numbers. From *Zi* to *Si* is yang; from *Wu* to *Hai* is yin—this is two sixes, divided by generation and completion. From *Zi* to *Xu* is yang; from *Chou* to *Hai* is yin—this is also two sixes, divided by odd and even. Twelve yin and yang each form half, splitting one into two and dividing the twelve. Four threes and two sixes: the four seasons each split into three, further dividing the two sixes. Twenty-four corresponds to the twelve qi of the months. Eight nodes: one node has three qi. Four seasons: one season has six qi.

The lines of the eight trigrams in Prior Heaven’s one palace each total forty-eight, divided among the four directions to correspond to the four phases.

The central void of twelve corresponds to earth, aligning with the four directions. In *Jiazi*, it holds twelve; in *Zhouyi*, one hexagram; in *Kun*, twelve yang remain; in *Qian*, twelve yin remain. Forty-eight is twelve. Subtract twelve and use thirty-six as old yang. From *Yin* to *Xu*, three are used and one unused—twenty-four: remove four sixes and use four sixes as old yin. From *Mao* to *Shen*, remove six and use six, each half. Twenty-eight: remove four fives and use four sevens. Thirty-two: remove four fours and use four eights. Whether from the middle of *Yin* to the middle of *Xu*, or from *Mao* to *You*, the used always exceeds the unused, marking the advance and retreat of *Qian* and *Kun*. These twelve numbers divide day and night, and the moon’s waxing and waning. Advancing twelve days, yang gains; retreating twelve days, yin contracts. When yang gains, the surplus of qi divides six into one hundred twenty; when yin contracts, the deficiency of qi also divides six into one hundred twenty. Six days advance, sixty days advance—paired, they make twenty-four—hence the use of two hundred forty-two, two hundred fifty-two, and two hundred sixty-four. One year has sixty *Jiazi*; small, it is six hours; large, six days. Even larger, sixty years—all twelve. Thus it is said: "Six *Jia* exhaust the heavenly Dao," and the moon uses thirty days as its mean. The midpoint of half a day is the conjunction of sun and moon. Excluding intercalary months also aligns with the numbers of one palace—though none have spoken of this before. *Qian* uses nine, *Kun* uses six. *Qian* and *Kun* advance and retreat within seven, eight, nine, and six. The body is four, the function six; *Qian* and *Kun* encompass both body and function. Thus thirty-six, transformed by four, becomes four nines; transformed by six, six sixes. Twenty-four, transformed by four, becomes four sixes; transformed by six, six fours. As for twenty-eight and thirty-two, they transform only by four and cannot transform by six.

From the perspective of function: four sixes make twenty-four, the extreme of yin. Advancing six makes thirty, the middle of yang; advancing another six makes thirty-six, the extreme of yang. Six sixes make thirty-six, the extreme of yang. Retreating six makes thirty, the middle of yin; retreating another six makes twenty-four, the extreme of yin. From the perspective of body: six fours make twenty-four, the extreme of yin. Advancing four makes twenty-eight, then another four makes thirty-two, then another four makes thirty-six, old yang. Nine fours make thirty-six, the extreme of yang. Retreating four makes thirty-two, then another four twenty-eight, then another four twenty-four, old yin. Only *Qian* and *Kun* can advance and retreat, uniquely converging within seven, eight, nine, and six—used as the two elders of yin and yang. The six children cannot transform by six, so their use is not discussed.

Yang arises within yin, advancing from six to nine; old yin arises within yang. Retreating from nine to six, the changes of the two elders never depart from the four images. Thus, adding four to nine, eight, seven, and six yields the body’s numbers of four. Further deducing function from within the body, we have thirty-six, thirty-two, twenty-eight, and twenty-four. The *Yi* has sixty-four hexagrams: sixty correspond to the six *Jia*, and four to the four seasons. The two elders and two youths each have their offices, yet yin can never precede yang. *Qian* is originally the number of six yangs, yet it can also incorporate half of *Kun* to become nine. Three threes make nine; nine nines, eighty-one. This is the number of old yang, beginning at three and culminating at nine. The numbers of old yin and the two youths are but nodes within it. Thus it is said: speaking of the body of one qi, it is called *Qian*, encompassing all.

The great *Yi* doubles its eighteen to divide the classic, totaling thirty-six. King Wen ordered it, Confucius aided it—revealing the utmost to humanity. Since the Han, none have been able to expound it. The *Jingshi* text doubles its two sixes to divide the epochs, totaling three hundred sixty. The great and small epochs, six advances and six retreats, manifest in years, months, days, and hours.

Zhang Guanwu said: The numerical method of twelve originates from the qi numbers of yin and yang, then divides. Three hundred eighty-four is the number of the body; three hundred sixty, the number of function. Ten uses seven, twelve uses eight—these are intersecting numbers. Yang gains six, yin contracts six—these are surplus numbers. One, three, five, seven, nine; two, four, six, eight, ten—these are the numbers of odd and even. Long numbers extend the small to the great, returning to *Qian*. Fractional numbers divide the great into the small, gestating into *Kun*. Further dividing one line of *Qian* descends into six hexagrams: *Dayou*, *Xiaoxu*, *Lü*, *Tongren*, and *Dun*—these are the images of *Qian*.

Multiplying numbers: two multiplied by twelve always ends at two; three multiplied by three advances to thirty, always ending at six. Dividing numbers: divide one into two, two into four, four into sixteen. Subtracting numbers are diminishing numbers. Multiplying numbers are extending numbers. For example, yin multiplying yang, yang multiplying yin—three hundred sixty multiplied by three hundred sixty—yields one hundred nineteen thousand six hundred, as in one *yuan*.

It is also said: Hexagrams have a body derived from function, and function derived from body. The body derived from function begins with one yin and one yang, becoming two yins and two yangs, then four yins and four yangs. Four becomes eight, combining into twelve yins and twelve yangs. In the *Prior Heaven Diagram*, the outer eight hexagrams descend from eight: eight yangs interspersed with eight yins, eight becoming sixteen.

Sixteen yins interspersed with sixteen yangs, sixteen becoming thirty-two. Thirty-two yins interspersed with thirty-two yangs, thirty-two becoming sixty-four. One hundred ninety-two yangs with eighty yins, one hundred ninety-two yins with eighty yangs. Taken together, the left side of the inner palace has sixty-four yangs and thirty-two yins, while the right side likewise has sixty-four yins and thirty-two yangs. In the upper palace, left and right each have forty-eight yangs and forty-eight yins. From body to function: from sixty-four to thirty-two, thirty-two to sixteen, sixteen to eight, eight to four, four to two, two to one. The One is the Supreme Polarity. This is the division of the Supreme Polarity, the Two Modes, the Four Images, and the Eight Trigrams.

Master Shao said: The body of Heaven and Earth has the number four, its function is three, and what is not used is one. He also said: Heaven’s four transformations contain Earth’s four transformations. Heaven and Earth each have four trigrams; the eight are merely four. Heaven is round and takes function as its master, while its body is subsumed under Earth. Earth is square and takes body as its master, while its function follows Heaven. Heaven pares four down to three, taking three as its function. Earth splits one into four, taking four as its body. From *yin* to *xu*, three are used and one is not—this is the old yang of four nines. From *mao* to *shen*, half are used and half are not—this is the old yin of four sixes. Four times four makes sixteen positions. Forms have the four directions, *qi* has the four seasons, and Heaven has the Four Images. Their transformations become cold and heat, day and night; containing Earth’s Four Images, they transform into rain, wind, dew, and thunder. Heaven is sufficient to envelop Earth. Heaven’s three doubled makes six, and six arises from one. Including the root makes seven; excluding the root makes six. Thus yang always preserves one to govern advance, advancing to thirty-six. Earth’s two uses twelve, and twelve arises from four. Including the root makes sixteen; excluding the root makes twelve. Thus yin always obscures one to govern retreat, retreating twelve months to diminish twelve days.

Therefore, the great ultimate of Heaven turns rightward from Earth, while the primordial *qi* of Earth moves leftward from Heaven. It is also said: Three is thirty, and one-one is two sixes. This speaks of the numerical reckoning of yin and yang *qi* in one year. One year has four seasons, one season has three months, and one month has three decades. Following Heaven’s function with the heavenly stems: five days make one *hou*, and three *hou* (fifteen days) make one *qi*. Following Earth’s function with the earthly branches: six days make one *fen*, and three *fen* (twelve hours) make one day. In the large, one year encompasses three hundred sixty days, divided from thirty days. In the small, one month encompasses three hundred sixty hours, accumulated from thirty *fen*. One day transforms into thirty, one *hui* has thirty *yun*, and one *shi* has thirty years. Thirty twelve-hour periods make one month, twelve thirty-day periods make one year, thirty twelve-month periods make one *shi*, twelve thirty-year periods make one *yun*, thirty twelve-*shi* periods make one *hui*, and twelve thirty-*yun* periods make one *yuan*.

It is also said: Heaven’s six transformations generate three hundred sixty—this is the number of its movement. One transformation generates six, two transformations generate twelve, three transformations generate eighteen, four transformations generate twenty-four, five transformations generate thirty, and six transformations generate thirty-six. Thereupon, advancing to three hundred sixty. The number of Heaven’s movement takes one as its root. Using one with six requires no reliance on Earth. One transformation is sixty, and six transformations are three hundred sixty—this is spoken in terms of Heaven and Earth. Five generates six: one month has five trigrams, and one trigram has six lines. Five multiplied by six—five sixes—makes thirty. Excluding the four cardinal trigrams, one year has sixty trigrams, and six sixes make three hundred sixty lines. One year completes sixty *jiazi* cycles, also six sixes making three hundred sixty days. One transformation generates six; subtract one to make five, and five takes one as its root. Two transformations generate twelve; subtract two to make ten, and ten takes two as its root. Extending to three, four, five, and six transformations, always subtract their three, four, five, or six to preserve the root, yielding the numbers fifteen, twenty, twenty-five, and thirty. Thus it is said: Five sixes generate thirty. Thirty trigrams correspond to Heaven’s six transformations, yielding one hundred eighty. In the *Prior Heaven Diagram*, left and right are alike, each having five transformations generating thirty-two yangs and thirty-two yins. Five and six alternate, odd and even pair, and thus five and six are the central numbers of Heaven and Earth. The movement of the four seasons goes nowhere without harmonizing with them.

Counting trigrams with the twelve branches, one transformation occurs every six days. Counting *hou* with the ten stems, one transformation occurs every five days. Sixty transformations generate three hundred sixty. Three hundred sixty multiplied by three hundred sixty yields the number of one *yuan*: one hundred twenty-nine thousand six hundred.

It is also said: Earth’s four transformations generate thirty-six—this is the number of generating things. Four generates twelve, twelve generates twenty, twenty generates twenty-eight, twenty-eight generates thirty-six, and thereupon advancing to two hundred fifty-six. The number of Earth’s generation takes four as its root and uses two with ten. Two splits one into four, splits four into sixteen, splits sixteen into sixty-four, and splits sixty-four into two hundred fifty-six—these are Earth’s four transformations. Sixteen is Earth’s four. One transformation into four is Earth’s one. Four generates eight: one four generates two fours, and combining them makes three fours—twelve.

Eight generates twelve: two fours generate three fours, and combining them yields five fours—twenty. Twelve generates sixteen: three fours generate four fours, and combining them yields four sevens—twenty-eight. Sixteen generates twenty: four fours generate five fours, and combining them yields four nines—thirty-six. Earth employs four transformations to reach nine, thereby generating things. Counting by six sixes governs Heaven’s movements; counting by four nines governs Earth’s generation

A *hui* comprises thirty *yun*, totaling 46,656,000 *shi* and 1,399,680,000 *fen*, which amounts to 16,799,160,000 *miao*, corresponding to the *Lǚ* hexagram. A *yuan* comprises twelve *hui*, totaling 559,872,000 *shi* and 16,799,160,000 *fen*, which amounts to 201,553,920,000 *miao*, corresponding to the *Duì* hexagram. The number 129,600 constitutes a *yuan*: the years of a *yuan*, the months of a *hui*, the days of a *yun*, and the *chen* of a *shi* all share this number of 129,600.

The sixty *jiazi* cycle circulates within the Prior Heaven’s square and circular diagrams. The circular diagram represents Heaven; removing the four cardinal hexagrams and their twenty-four lines corresponds to 360 days, moving through the ten Celestial Stems and twelve Earthly Branches. The ten Stems correspond to Heaven’s ten days, while the twelve Branches correspond to Earth’s twelve months and twelve *shi*. Thus, five days make a *hou*, ten days make a *jia*, fifteen days make a *qi*, and thirty days make a month. *Jia* and *wu* transform through yang, *ji* and *gui* through yin—five transformations. *Wu* and *hai* transform through yin, *zi* and *si* through yang—six transformations. In a year, the *jiazi* cycle completes six-tenths; in a month, three *jia* cycles with five-sixths of another; in a year, thirty-six *jia* cycles yielding 360 movements, revolving through Heaven’s five to generate seventy-two. In a month, two *zi* with half of another, five-sixths of six; in a year, three sets of ten *zi*, also totaling 360 movements, revolving through Earth’s six to likewise complete seventy-two. On the left of the diagram, fifteen *zi*. Each *zi* undergoes two transformations, totaling thirty transformations—1, 3, 6, 180. The right is the same, also totaling 360. Thirty *fen* make a *shi*; 360 make the *miao* of a *shi*; 4,300 accumulate into a day. Again, taking months as years, two and a half days and thirty *shi* make a month. The thirty *fen* of a *shi*—each *fen* as a day, every *fen* with twelve *miao*, each *miao* as a *shi*. Condensing years into months, months into days, days into *shi*. Even 129,600 years are but the accumulation of the *fen* and *miao* of a single *shi*. Divided minutely, it extends to 16,799,616,000 *miao* and no further. Refined ever further, it enables the investigation of principles and the exhaustion of affairs. Ascending into the azure heavens, descending into the yellow springs, broadly containing primordial *qi*, minutely entering the boundless.

Master Yang Xiong once deduced this. Now, rotating the circular diagram reveals the expansion and contraction of emperors, kings, and hegemons; the order and chaos of past and present; the movements of the four seasons and myriad transformations; the revolutions of the sun, moon, and stars. *Qian* and *Kun* govern it, thereby illuminating Heaven’s numbers.

The square diagram represents Earth, structured by four. Counting by fours, reaching four nines, it turns to sixteen matters for clarification, extending to 256 positions for differentiation. Heaven’s voice initiates above as the six *lü* resonate; Earth’s tone responds below as the six *lü* answer. Creatures that run, fly, and plants all correspond to these numbers. *Kan* and *Li* govern its movements, with four yin and four yang generating beings on Earth.

The Prior Heaven’s study begins from the center of the diagram. The great pivot of creation is all the marvel of spontaneity. Master Shao should have contemplated this with profound insight, never departing from it even for a day. Master Cheng said: *"The Book of Changes* reckons in reverse. To foresee the unmanifest as if it were past, what need is there for divination?" Yet numbers are principle. Principle has its inevitabilities, such as the three or five generations. Rarely does it err—numbers cannot escape principle. Since the Qin and Han dynasties, abandoning principle to speak of numbers has long led to apocrypha. Only Master Kangjie spoke of numbers to reach principle, aligning with the movements of Heaven and Earth. Effortlessly compliant, vast in its return.
